Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
8 min
The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on Exception in Numbers
Analyses the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute over exception in numbers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on exception in numbers, explain the Hanafi proof that 'ten except three' remains literal, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf in contracts and oaths.

Core Idea
Exception in numbers does not make the number figurative; 'ten except three' is a literal qualified composite.

How should we understand a phrase like 'ten except three'? Does 'ten' become a metaphor for 'seven', or does it remain literal? This question, debated between Hanafi and Shafi'i scholars, reveals deep principles about language, logic, and legal interpretation. In this lesson, we will unpack the arguments and see why the Hanafi school insists on the literal meaning.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i position
Identify the Shafi'i claim: 'ten' in 'ten except three' is used figuratively to mean 'seven', with the exception serving as a contextual clue (qarinah) diverting from literal to figurative meaning.
The Shafi'is view exception as creating an opposing ruling that necessitates figurative interpretation.
2
Understand the Hanafi criticism
Analyze the Hanafi refutation: numbers are precise terms (mawdu'ah) that cannot be used for other quantities; the opposition theory would lead to contradiction and make the exceptive phrase redundant (laghw).
The Hanafis argue that exception is a qualification, not a figurative reinterpretation.
3
Explain the Hanafi alternative
Describe the Hanafi analysis: 'ten' is a composite of seven and three; the exception subtracts three, leaving a true qualified composite 'ten minus three', which is literal and logical.
This preserves the literal meaning of 'ten' while accounting for the subtraction.
4
Apply to a practical example
Consider a contract: 'I give you ten dirhams except three.' Under the Hanafi view, seven dirhams are owed; under the Shafi'i view, the contract may be problematic due to figurative speech.
This thamarah al-khilaf shows the real-world impact of the linguistic dispute.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text clearly sides with the Hanafi position, stating 'I say: this is the correct view' and providing extensive arguments. Note the reliance on logical analysis and rejection of metaphor.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.

مسألة
(قد اختلف في نحو علي عشرة إلا ثلاثة دفعاً للتناقض المتوهم بين ثبوت العشرة وبين إخراج الثلاثة عنها (فالجمهور) من الشافعية قالوا المراد بعشرة إنما هو السبعة) مجازاً (وإلاّ ثلاثة قرينة عليه صارفة عن حقيقتها إلى مجازها اعلم أن مشايخنا حكوا عن الشافعي رضي الله عنه أن الاستثناء يدفع عن بعض المستثنى منه بطريق المعارضة، وفسره بعضهم بأن الحكم في المستثنى منه على الكل ثم المستثنى يفيد حكماً معارضاً له في البعض، وإذا تعارضا تساقطا ويبقى في الباقي حكم المستثنى منه ، وهذا ليس بشيء، فإنه مع كونه باطلاً في نفسه وموجباً للتناقض في الإخبار يوجب أن لا يكون في المستثنى الحكم المخالف لحكم الصدر، وهو خلاف تصريحات الشافعية، وقال صدر الشريعة : حاصله أن المراد بالصدر الباقي مجازا والاستثناء قرينة ولعله إلى هذا أشار بقوله كسائر المخصصات وتحقيقه أن الاستثناء يفيد حكماً معارضاً للظاهر من حكم الصدر، فلأجل هذا يحكم العقل أن المراد في الصدر سواه كالمخصصات المستقلة، فالاستثناء بحكمه قرينة صارفة إلى التخصيص ثم أبطل هو رحمه الله تعالى أن هذا لا يصح في أسماء العدد فإن عشرة مثلاً موضوعة لعدد مخصوص لا يحتمل أن يطلق على ما تحته أو ما فوقه من المراتب العددية أصلاً، فلا يجوز أن يراد به الباقي، ولو سلم فيكون مجازاً وهو خلاف الأصل وسيجيء ما له وما عليه إن شاء الله تعالى. فإن قلت: قد أبطل المشايخ الكرام القول بالمعارضة بأنه يلزم التناقض في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَبِثَ فِيهِمْ أَلْفَ سَنَةٍ إلا خمسين عاما ﴾ [العنكبوت : ٦٤] وهذا إنما يستقيم لو فسر بالتفسير الأول لا الثاني كما لا يخفى، قلت : تقريره على الثاني بأن يقال : اسم العدد لا يحتمل إطلاقه على الأقل، فلا يحمل الألف على تسعمائة وخمسين فيبقى الحكم على الأول مع ثبوت نقيضه في البعض فتأمل فيه، فإنه ينبو عنه ظواهر عبارات المشايخ (أقول : وهو الصحيح لأن تناول اللفظ) المستثنى منه للمستثنى (باق) بعد الاستثناء كما كان قبل فإن العشرة مفهوم واحد لا يزيد ولا ينقص، فهو من حيث هو هو لا يمكن أن يتصف بإخراج الثلاثة منها فلو كان العشرة باقية على الحقيقة لما الاستثناء والإخراج فهو مستعمل في سبعة بقرينة الاستثناء، فإن قلت : لا نسلم أن العشرة حقيقة لا يزيد ولا ينقص، بل السبعة أيضاً من أفراد العشرة ، ألا ترى أن أهل المنطق قالوا : الإنسان الذي ليس بحيوان من أفراد الإنسان واحتاجوا إلى إخراجه بقيد الإمكان، ولو لم يكن من أفراده لما احتاجوا إلى التقييد قال وما قالوا في تحقيق القضية (الحقيقية) الحاكمة على الأفراد مطلقاً فرضية كانت أو موجودة (إن الإنسان الذي ليس بحيوان بل) الذي (ليس بإنسان من الأفراد الفرضية للإنسان، وقيدوا في الأفراد بالإمكان لخروجه فهو مخالف للعرف واللغة) وكلامنا فيما يرضيان به والمنع مكابرة بل مخالف للعقل أيضاً كما قال بعض المحققين إن الفرد للكلي حقيقة ما يصدق هو عليه في نفس الأمر بالفعل أو بالإمكان، وليس الإنسان الذي ليس بحيوان مما يصدق عليه الحيوان أصلاً، قد يكون فرداً له حقيقة (ولو سلم الاتصاف) أي اتصاف العشرة بالزيادة والنقصان فلا يمنع التناول للثلاثة (أيضاً) فيلزم أن يكون مخرجاً عنه وغير مخرج على تقدير أن تكون العشرة باقية على الحقيقة، وذلك لأن العشرة عشرة أطلق أو قيد ولو كان التقييد (بالنقيض ) كما إذا قيد بخروج الثلاثة ونقصانه إلى السبعة كيف لا وثبوت الذاتيات للذات ضروري في مرتبة (الذات فلا يبطل الذاتي بالتقييد البتة هذا وما قالوا: العدد لا يكون جزءاً لعدد لا ينافيه فإن المراد أن ثلاثة آحاد جزء للعدد فيكون ثابتاً في مرتبة الذات، فلا يجوز أن لا يتناول واعلم أن هذا غير واف فإنه لا شك عند أحد في أنه إذا حل مركب ثم نقص عنه جزء يبقى الجزء الآخر، ألا ترى أن النبات إذا انحل وبطل نفسه النباتي يبقى الجزء الجسمي قطعاً، وكذلك في الذهن إذا حلل المعلوم المركب إلى جزأين وطرح أحدهما يبقى الآخر، فإذا أخذ الذهن عشرة وحللها إلى سبعة وثلاثة وأسقط الثلاثة يبقى قطعاً، ويصدق عليه أن العشرة إذا نقصت عنها ثلاثة صارت سبعة أي الذي كان عشرة يبقى منه بعد التنقيص سبعة، فيصدق على السبعة أنه عشرة منقوص منها ثلاثة في العرف واللغة، وإن لم يصدق عليه أنه عشرة فإن صدق المقيد لغة لا يستلزم صدق المطلق فيعبر بهذا المقيد عن السبعة كما يعبر عنها بلفظها فبإزائه عبارة أطول وأقصر فللمعبر أن يعبر بأيهما شاء، وحينئذ اندفع ما قال المصنف فإنه إن أراد أن العشرة لا يزيد ولا ينقص أن حقيقتها لا تبقى بعد الزيادة والنقصان بل تصير حقيقة عدد آخر فمسلم لكن لا يلزم منه أن يكون لفظ العشرة مجازاً عن السبعة، بل لفظ العشرة على الحقيقة، وحكم عليه بتنقيص بعض الأجزاء عنه وهو الثلاثة مثلاً وبقاء الجزء السبعة والمركب التقييدي يصدق عليه وإن أراد أن العشرة لا تتحمل هذه التصرفات فباطل قطعاً، وبهذا ظهر اندفاع ما في «التحرير» أنه حينئذ يلزم اللغو في الكلام، فإن ذكر الأفراد والحكم على البعض مما لم يوجد في الاستعمال ومسافة طويلة مع إمكان التعبير جميع عن البعض بلفظ دال عليه وجه الاندفاع أن الدال عليه عبارتان أطول وأقصر، والمتكلم مخير بأيهما شاء يتكلم كما إن شاء يقول : الإنسان ماش وإن شاء قال : الحيوان الناطق ماش، فكذا ههنا إن شاء عبر عن السبعة بلفظ السبعة وإن شاء فبلفظ عشرة إلا ثلاثة، ثم إنه لو صح المذهب أي القول بأن العشرة مجاز عن السبعة لزم اللغو قطعاً كيف لا وإذا كان العشرة بمعنى السبعة فأي معنى لقوله إلا ثلاثة فإن إلا للإخراج قطعاً بإطباق أهل اللغة، فالمستثنى الأداة لغو قطعاً، فإن قلت : إنه قرينة على أن المراد بها السبعة ولولاه لما علم، قلت: هب مع أنه قرينة لكن القرينة لا تكون مهملة وههنا تصير الأداة مع المستثنى مهملاً، والسر فيه أن الاستثناء لما كان غير مستقل يقتضي الارتباط مع ما قبله وإذا صار ما قبله بمعنى السبعة فلا الارتباط به فيلغو قطعاً، وحينئذ لا يتوجه ما لو قيل إن الاستثناء يدل على حكم معارض يصح لحكم المستثنى منه فمعنى إلا ثلاثة ليس عليّ ثلاثة وبه تبين أن المراد بالعشرة السبعة كما في سائر المخصصات، كما يعزى إلى الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى فلا يكون الاستثناء مهملاً، وذلك لأن غير المستقل لا يفيد معنى من غير أن يرتبط بما قبله وهذا ظاهر جداً وإذا أريد بالعشرة السبعة لا أن يرتبط به إلا ثلاثة فلا يفيد شيئاً وهذا بخلاف المخصص، فإنه لاستقلاله يفيد حكماً مخالفاً للعام فيدل على أنه مخصوص ثم إن ما يعزى إلى الإمام الشافعي
The third article on linguistic principles. Issue: (There is disagreement regarding expressions like 'ten except three' to avoid the apparent contradiction between affirming ten and removing three from it. (The majority) of Shafi'is said: what is meant by 'ten' is only 'seven' metaphorically, and 'except three' is a contextual clue diverting from its literal meaning to its metaphorical. Know that our shaykhs narrated from al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him, that exception repels from some of the excepted-from by way of opposition. Some interpreted it: the ruling in the excepted-from applies to all, then the exception provides a ruling opposing it in part, and when they conflict they cancel each other, and the ruling of the excepted-from remains in the remainder. This is nothing; besides being invalid in itself and causing contradiction in the statement, it entails that the excepted part does not have the ruling contrary to the first part, contrary to explicit statements of the Shafi'is. Sadr al-Shari'ah said: its gist is that what is intended by the first part is the remainder metaphorically, and the exception is a contextual clue. Perhaps he alluded to this by his saying 'like other general-specifiers'. Its verification: the exception provides a ruling contrary to the apparent ruling of the first part; therefore reason judges that what is meant in the first part is other than it, like independent specifiers. So the exception by its ruling is a diverting clue to specification. Then he, may Allah have mercy on him, refuted that this is not valid for number-nouns, for 'ten' for example is placed for a specific number that cannot be applied to what is below or above it among numerical ranks at all; thus it is not permissible to intend the remainder by it. If conceded, it would be metaphorical, contrary to the principle, and what he has and what is against him will come, Allah willing. If you say: the noble shaykhs refuted the claim of opposition by the necessity of contradiction in His statement: 'Then he stayed among them a thousand years except fifty years' (al-'Ankabut 29:14). This only holds if interpreted by the first interpretation, not the second, as is clear. I say: its formulation according to the second: number-noun does not admit application to the lesser, so 'thousand' is not taken as nine hundred and fifty, so the ruling on the first remains while its contrary is established in part; reflect on it, for the apparent expressions of the shaykhs recoil from it. I say: the correct view is that the word's coverage of the excepted from the excepted-from remains after exception as it was before, for 'ten' is a single concept that neither increases nor decreases; as such it cannot be described as removing three from it. So if 'ten' remained literally, what would be the purpose of exception and removal? It is used for seven by the contextual clue of exception. If you say: we do not concede that 'ten' is a reality that neither increases nor decreases; rather seven is also an individual of ten. Do you not see that the logicians said: 'human that is not animal' is an individual of human, and they needed to remove it by the condition of possibility; if it were not an individual they would not need the qualification. They said in verifying the true proposition that judges over individuals absolutely, whether hypothetical or actual: 'human that is not animal' but 'that is not human' are among the hypothetical individuals of human, and they qualified by possibility to exclude it. That contradicts custom and language, and our discussion concerns what both accept. Denial is obstinacy, rather contradictory to reason. As some investigators said: the individual of a universal is truly what it is actually predicated of in actual fact, potentially or actually; 'human that is not animal' is not something that 'animal' is predicated of at all; it may be an individual of it truly. (Even if the description is conceded) i.e., describing 'ten' as increase and decrease, it does not prevent coverage of the three, so it would be both excluded and not excluded on the assumption that 'ten' remains literal. That is because 'ten' is ten whether unrestricted or qualified, even if the qualification is by the opposite, such as when qualified by removal of three and reduction to seven. How not? The subsistence of essentials for the essence is necessary in the essence's rank; thus the essential is not nullified by qualification at all. Their saying: a number is not part of a number does not contradict this, for what is meant is that three units are part of the number, so it is established in the essence's rank, so it cannot not be covered. Know that this is insufficient, for there is no doubt that when a composite is dissolved and a part is removed from it, the other part remains. Do you not see that when a plant dissolves and its 'plantness' ceases, the bodily part remains absolutely? Similarly in the mind, when the composite known is analyzed into two parts and one is discarded, the other remains. So when the mind takes ten and analyzes it into seven and three, and drops the three, the seven remains absolutely; and it is true of it that ten when reduced by three becomes seven, i.e., what was ten remains after reduction as seven. So it is true of seven, in custom and language, that it is 'ten minus three', even if it is not true that it is 'ten'. For the truth of the qualified expression in language does not entail the truth of the unqualified; so this qualified expression expresses seven just as its own word does. So there are two expressions, one longer and one shorter, and the speaker may express by whichever he wishes. Hence what the author said is refuted: if he meant that ten neither increases nor decreases, i.e., its reality does not remain after increase or decrease but becomes the reality of another number, that is granted, but it does not entail that the word 'ten' is metaphorical for seven; rather the word 'ten' is literal, and it is ruled upon as having some parts removed, namely three, and the part seven remains; and the qualified composite is true of it. If he meant that 'ten' cannot undergo these operations, that is false absolutely. By this it appears that what is in al-Tahrir is refuted: that then linguistic uselessness would result, for mentioning the individuals and ruling on some is not found in usage, and it is a long route despite the possibility of expressing the part by a word denoting it. The way of refutation: the denoting expressions are two, longer and shorter, and the speaker may choose whichever. For example, one may say 'human walks' or 'rational animal walks'. Similarly here, he may express seven by the word 'seven' or by 'ten except three'. Moreover, if the doctrine were sound—i.e., the saying that 'ten' is metaphorical for seven—then uselessness would follow absolutely. How not? If 'ten' means seven, what meaning is left for 'except three'? For 'except' is for exclusion, by consensus of linguists; thus the exceptive tool becomes useless. If you say: it is a contextual clue that the intended is seven; without it it would not be known. I say: even if it is a clue, the clue is not disregarded; here the tool together with the excepted becomes disregarded. The reason is that exception, being dependent, requires connection with what precedes; if what precedes becomes meaning seven, there is no connection, so it becomes useless. Hence the argument that exception indicates a contrary ruling valid for the ruling of the excepted-from, and that the meaning of 'except three' is 'not three', so it becomes clear that the intended by 'ten' is seven, as in other specifiers, as attributed to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, so that exception is not disregarded—this does not hold. For the dependent element does not convey meaning without being connected to what precedes; this is very clear. If 'ten' means seven, 'except three' cannot connect to it meaningfully. This is different from the specifier, for it is independent and conveys a ruling contrary to the general, indicating that it is specified. Then what is attributed to Imam al-Shafi'i...
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed usul al-fiqh dispute regarding the nature of exception (istithna') when applied to numbers like 'ten except three'. The core issue is whether such expressions involve figurative language (majaz) or remain literal (haqiqah). The Shafi'i position, attributed to Imam al-Shafi'i by the Hanafi shuyukh, is that the exception creates a ruling that opposes the apparent meaning of the first part (the mustathna minhu). According to this view, the first part (e.g., 'ten') is understood metaphorically to refer to the remainder (seven), with the exception serving as a contextual clue (qarinah) diverting from literal to figurative. The Hanafi scholars, particularly Sadr al-Shari'ah and the author of this sharh, strongly refute this. They argue that numbers like 'ten' are precise terms that cannot be used for any other quantity; they are 'mawdu'ah' for a specific number. Therefore, 'ten' cannot metaphorically mean seven. The Hanafi alternative is that the exception does not change the meaning of 'ten'; instead, the statement 'ten except three' is a true literal statement about a composite: ten is a composite of seven and three, and the exception subtracts the three, leaving seven as the actual referent of the qualified expression. This is not metaphorical but a logical analysis: the mind decomposes the ten into parts. The Hanafis emphasize that this is the view consistent with language and reason. They further argue that if 'ten' were metaphorical for seven, then the exceptive phrase would become redundant (laghw), as 'except three' would add no meaning—a conclusion they deem unacceptable. The passage also addresses the logical argument from the Quranic verse (29:14) where 'a thousand years except fifty' would be contradictory under the Shafi'i reading if interpreted as the first interpretation (opposition causing cancellation). The Hanafis uphold that the verse remains a true statement without contradiction. This dispute illustrates a key Hanafi usul principle: exception is a form of specification (takhsis) that operates on the literal meaning without rendering it figurative.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithnā'): A grammatical and legal tool used to exclude something from a general statement, e.g., 'except three' in 'ten except three'.
مجاز (majāz): A word used in a non-literal sense due to a contextual clue (qarinah). The Shafi'is claim 'ten' in 'ten except three' is majaz for 'seven'.
حقيقة (ḥaqīqah): A word used in its original, literal sense. The author argues that 'ten' remains haqiqah in 'ten except three'.
قرينة (qarīnah): A contextual clue that guides interpretation. The Shafi'is see 'except three' as a qarinah for figurative meaning; the Hanafis see it as a qualifier of the literal meaning.
مخصص (mukhassis): An independent specifier that restricts a general term. The text contrasts exception (dependent) with independent specifiers like 'except' vs. a separate statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, how is the phrase 'ten except three' (عشرة إلا ثلاثة) correctly interpreted?
A) 'Ten' is used metaphorically to mean 'seven', and 'except three' is a contextual clue.
B) 'Ten' remains literal, and the expression means 'ten minus three', which is a true qualified composite referring to seven.
C) 'Ten' and 'except three' are contradictory, so the statement is invalid.
D) The exception cancels the number, leaving an unspecified quantity.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, exception in numbers is a qualification, not a figurative reinterpretation; 'ten except three' is a literal composite expression.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
15 min
The Hanafi Defense of 'Ten Except Three': Metaphor or Real Usage?
Detailed refutation of the metaphorical interpretation of exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two competing interpretations of exception (istithna') and apply the Hanafi argument that the excepted-from remains in its real meaning.

Core Idea
In 'ten except three', 'ten' is real; the composite phrase does the work of referring to seven.

This passage from a commentary on Muslim al-Thubut addresses a classic usul dispute: when we say 'ten except three', does the word 'ten' become a metaphor for 'seven'? The Hanafi school insists that 'ten' retains its real meaning of ten, and the exception merely qualifies it. The author refutes the opposing attribution to al-Shafi'i with linguistic and rational proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two views
State the Hanafi position: 'ten' is used in its real, complete meaning. State the opposing view (attributed to al-Shafi'i): 'ten' is a metaphor for 'seven'.
The difference hinges on whether the exception particle 'illa' is meaningful or redundant.
2
Analyze the Hanafi argument from qualification
The author argues that a qualified expression (e.g., 'ten reduced by three') can truthfully apply to seven without 'ten' being a metaphor. The truth of the qualified does not require the absolute to be false.
This is based on the linguistic principle that 'truth of the qualified does not entail truth of the absolute'.
3
Examine the redundancy objection
If 'ten' meant 'seven', then 'except three' would be redundant because it would not be excluding anything from 'ten'. The Hanafi response is that language allows both longer and shorter expressions; the speaker may choose.
Analogous to saying 'rational animal' instead of 'human'.
4
Evaluate the absurd consequences
The author shows that if the metaphor view were generalized, phrases like 'a thousand except four' would require mental gymnastics to interpret, contradicting customary understanding.
This reductio ad absurdum strengthens the Hanafi position.
5
Summarize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference lies in legal contexts (e.g., acknowledgments, contracts). The Hanafi view preserves clarity: the general term remains general, and the exception narrows it without changing the original term's meaning.
This ensures consistency in interpretation of exception across different cases.

الآخر وهو وغير مخرج على تقدير أن تكون العشرة باقية على الحقيقة، وذلك لأن العشرة عشرة أطلق أو قيد ولو كان التقييد (بالنقيض) كما إذا قيد بخروج الثلاثة ونقصانه إلى السبعة كيف لا وثبوت الذاتيات للذات ضروري في مرتبة (الذات فلا يبطل الذاتي بالتقييد البتة هذا وما قالوا: العدد لا يكون جزءاً لعدد لا ينافيه فإن المراد أن ثلاثة آحاد جزء للعدد فيكون ثابتاً في مرتبة الذات، فلا يجوز أن لا يتناول واعلم أن هذا غير واف فإنه لا شك عند أحد في أنه إذا حل مركب ثم نقص عنه جزء يبقى الجزء الآخر، ألا ترى أن النبات إذا انحل وبطل نفسه النباتي يبقى الجزء الجسمي قطعاً، وكذلك في الذهن إذا حلل المعلوم المركب إلى جزأين وطرح أحدهما يبقى الآخر، فإذا أخذ الذهن عشرة وحللها إلى سبعة وثلاثة وأسقط الثلاثة يبقى قطعاً، ويصدق عليه أن العشرة إذا نقصت عنها ثلاثة صارت سبعة أي الذي كان عشرة يبقى منه بعد التنقيص سبعة، فيصدق على السبعة أنه عشرة منقوص منها ثلاثة في العرف واللغة، وإن لم يصدق عليه أنه عشرة فإن صدق المقيد لغة لا يستلزم صدق المطلق فيعبر بهذا المقيد عن السبعة كما يعبر عنها بلفظها فبإزائه عبارة أطول وأقصر فللمعبر أن يعبر بأيهما شاء، وحينئذ اندفع ما قال المصنف فإنه إن أراد أن العشرة لا يزيد ولا ينقص أن حقيقتها لا تبقى بعد الزيادة والنقصان بل تصير حقيقة عدد آخر فمسلم لكن لا يلزم منه أن يكون لفظ العشرة مجازاً عن السبعة، بل لفظ العشرة على الحقيقة، وحكم عليه بتنقيص بعض الأجزاء عنه وهو الثلاثة مثلاً وبقاء الجزء السبعة والمركب التقييدي يصدق عليه وإن أراد أن العشرة لا تتحمل هذه التصرفات فباطل قطعاً، وبهذا ظهر اندفاع ما في «التحرير» أنه حينئذ يلزم اللغو في الكلام، فإن ذكر الأفراد والحكم على البعض مما لم يوجد في الاستعمال ومسافة طويلة مع إمكان التعبير جميع عن البعض بلفظ دال عليه وجه الاندفاع أن الدال عليه عبارتان أطول وأقصر، والمتكلم مخير بأيهما شاء يتكلم كما إن شاء يقول : الإنسان ماش وإن شاء قال : الحيوان الناطق ماش، فكذا ههنا إن شاء عبر عن السبعة بلفظ السبعة وإن شاء فبلفظ عشرة إلا ثلاثة، ثم إنه لو صح المذهب أي القول بأن العشرة مجاز عن السبعة لزم اللغو قطعاً كيف لا وإذا كان العشرة بمعنى السبعة فأي معنى لقوله إلا ثلاثة فإن إلا للإخراج قطعاً بإطباق أهل اللغة، فالمستثنى الأداة لغو قطعاً، فإن قلت : إنه قرينة على أن المراد بها السبعة ولولاه لما علم، قلت: هب مع أنه قرينة لكن القرينة لا تكون مهملة وههنا تصير الأداة مع المستثنى مهملاً، والسر فيه أن الاستثناء لما كان غير مستقل يقتضي الارتباط مع ما قبله وإذا صار ما قبله بمعنى السبعة فلا الارتباط به فيلغو قطعاً، وحينئذ لا يتوجه ما لو قيل إن الاستثناء يدل على حكم معارض يصح لحكم المستثنى منه فمعنى إلا ثلاثة ليس عليّ ثلاثة وبه تبين أن المراد بالعشرة السبعة كما في سائر المخصصات، كما يعزى إلى الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى فلا يكون الاستثناء مهملاً، وذلك لأن غير المستقل لا يفيد معنى من غير أن يرتبط بما قبله وهذا ظاهر جداً وإذا أريد بالعشرة السبعة لا أن يرتبط به إلا ثلاثة فلا يفيد شيئاً وهذا بخلاف المخصص، فإنه لاستقلاله يفيد حكماً مخالفاً للعام فيدل على أنه مخصوص ثم إن ما يعزى إلى الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى لو كان حقاً لكان المفهوم من قولنا له عليّ عشرة إلا ثلاثة عشرة لا ثلاثة منه أو ليس ما فوق سبعة إلى العشرة واحداً، وهو خلاف ما يفهم في العرف فافهم. ويلزم أن يكون في ألف إلا أربعة ألف إلا أربعة وخمسين الألف بمعنى تسعمائة وستة وأربعين مع أنه لا يلتفت إليه المتكلم ولا يفهم حين الاستعمال أصلاً، بل يحتاج إلى تأمل بالغ بعد معرفة معنى فافهم. واحفظ، فقد بان بطلان هذا القول بأقوم حجة لا يدحضها شبهة أصلاً، وظهر منه أيضاً أن لا تخصيص فيه بل العام المستثنى منه باقٍ على معناه والباقي إنما يفهم من المجموع بمعنى أنه يفهم معنى مركب يصدق على الباقي فهذا إنجاز ما وعدنا سابقاً، ثم إن المصنف لما اختار أن المراد من المستثنى منه الباقي فلا إخراج منه وأما الإخراج عن الحكم فلا يصح على رأي أحد أراد أن يحقق ذلك وقال ثم لا إخراج للمستثنى (عن الحكم على الكل) من المستثنى منه (أيضاً) كما أنه لا إخراج عنه إذ لا حكم إلا على السبعة (بالاتفاق فلا حكم على العشرة حتى يخرج منه اللزوم التناقض فإنه يلزم حينئذ أن يكون العشرة مثبتاً ومنفياً فلا إخراج عن الحكم) المذكور في الصدر (إلا) تقريراً بمعنى لولاه لدخل أي لولا الاستثناء لدخل المستثنى في الحكم (فالاستثناء يمنع الدخول) للمستثنى (في الحكم، فالعشرة إنما استعمل في التركيب لإفادة أن الحكم المذكور في الصدر (على السبعة فقط فتأمل جداً وهذا ظاهر، لكن طريقه أتي إما أن يكون العشرة على معناه والسبعة مستفاداً من المجموع، أو يكون مستعملاً في السبعة، الحق هو الأوّل، ومختار المصنف هو الثاني (واستدل على هذا المذهب (بأنه لا يراد بالعشرة كمالها لأنه ما أقر إلا بسبعة (اتفاقاً ولو كان العشرة بكمالها مرادة يلزم الإقرار بها (وأجيب بأن الإقرار إنما يكون (باعتبار الإسناد ولا إسناد إلا بعد الإخراج فكونه إقراراً بالسبعة لا يستلزم أن لا يكون العشرة على معناها فإن الإسناد إلى ما بقي بعد إخراج الثلاثة فلا تقريب فتأمل (وقال جماعة ومنهم الشيخ ابن الحاجب : المراد عشرة أفراد، لكن أخرج ثلاثة عنها ثم أسند إلى الباقي وهذا يحتمل وجهين : الأول : أنه يطلق العشرة على كمال معناها، وأسند إلى جزء معناها المفهوم في ضمنه وهو السبعة، الثاني: أن يقيد بإخراج الثلاثة عنها، فحصل مركب تقييدي هو العشرة المنقوص منها ثلاثة، وهو لا يصدق إلا على سبعة فيراد السبعة بهذا الوجه، فإن كان مراد ابن الحاجب الأول كما زعم صدر الشريعة منا وغيره فيلزم عليه اللغو، فإن ذكر البعض الآخر يلغو حينئذ، وإن أريد الثاني فهو حق غاية ما يلزم التعبير عن السبعة بطريق أطول ولا بأس به (أقول) في إبطاله قد لا يكون العموم المصحح للإخراج إلا بعد الإسناد) كما إذا وقع النكرة في سياق النفي (نحو : ما جاءني إلا زيد) وإذا كان العموم بعد الإسناد، فكيف يكون الإسناد بعد الإخراج (فتأمل) فإن فيه نظراً، أما أولاً فلأن هذا يرد عليكم أيضاً، فإن العام مخصوص عندكم قبل الإسناد وإلا لزم التناقض ولا عموم قبله فلا تخصيص جوابكم فهو جوابنا، وأما ثانياً : فلأن عموم النكرة المنفية عندنا بالوضع لا لأجل وقوع النفي عليه عقلاً، وإذا كان بالوضع فالذي يذكر بعد النفي، لأن تعلق النفي عام قبل الإسناد فيصح الإخراج، والمثال المذكور مفرغ فالمستثنى منه العام مقدر وهو كالملفوظ، وإليه فما هو
The other [view] and it is not excluded on the assumption that ten remains in its reality, because ten is ten whether absolute or qualified, even if the qualification is by the opposite, as when it is qualified by the exclusion of three and its decrease to seven. How not? The affirmation of essential attributes for the essence is necessary in the rank of essence, so the essential is not invalidated by qualification at all. This is what they said: number is not a part of number does not contradict it, for what is meant is that three units are a part of the number, so it is established in the rank of essence, thus it is not permissible that it does not encompass. Know that this is insufficient, for there is no doubt in anyone's mind that if a composite is dissolved and then a part is removed from it, the other part remains. Do you not see that if a plant disintegrates and its vegetative self ceases, the bodily part remains absolutely? Similarly in the mind, if the known composite is analyzed into two parts and one is discarded, the other remains. If the mind takes ten and analyzes it into seven and three and drops the three, it remains absolutely. And it is true of it that when ten has three removed from it, it becomes seven, i.e., that which was ten remains after reduction as seven. Thus, seven is described as ten from which three has been removed in custom and language, even if it is not described as ten. For the truth of the qualified in language does not entail the truth of the absolute. So this qualified expression is used for seven just as it is expressed by its own word, and opposite it is a longer and shorter expression, so the speaker may express with whichever he wishes. Then what the author said is repelled. For if he meant that ten does not increase or decrease, that its reality does not remain after increase and decrease but becomes the reality of another number, that is granted. But it does not entail that the word 'ten' is a metaphor for seven. Rather, the word 'ten' is in its reality, and it is ruled upon by the removal of some parts from it, namely three, and the survival of the part seven, and the qualified composite applies to it. And if he meant that ten does not bear these operations, it is absolutely false. By this the objection in al-Tahrir is repelled, that then there would be redundancy in speech, because mentioning the individuals and ruling on some is not found in usage, and a long distance despite the possibility of expressing all of the part by a word indicating it. The way of repelling it is that the indicator is two expressions, longer and shorter, and the speaker is free to speak with whichever he wishes, just as if he wishes he says: 'Man is walking' and if he wishes he says: 'The rational animal is walking.' So here, if he wishes he expresses seven by the word 'seven' and if he wishes by 'ten except three.' Then if the doctrine were correct, i.e., the statement that ten is a metaphor for seven, then redundancy would necessarily occur. How not? If ten means seven, what meaning is there for his saying 'except three'? For 'except' is for exclusion by the consensus of linguists, so the excepted tool is absolutely redundant. If you say: It is a context clue that the intended is seven, and without it it would not be known. I say: Granted that it is a context clue, but a context clue is not disregarded, yet here the tool along with the excepted becomes disregarded. The secret is that exception, being dependent, requires connection with what precedes it. If what precedes it becomes meaning seven, then there is no connection with it, so it is absolutely redundant. Then what is said that exception indicates a contradicting ruling that makes the ruling of the excepted-from valid, so the meaning of 'except three' is 'not upon me three', and by that it is clarified that the intended by ten is seven, as in other specifics, as is attributed to al-Shafiʿi (may Allah have mercy on him), so exception is not disregarded. That is because the dependent does not convey a meaning without being connected to what precedes it, and this is very obvious. If ten is intended to mean seven, then 'except three' cannot be connected to it, so it conveys nothing. This is unlike the specific, for it, being independent, conveys a ruling contrary to the general, so it indicates that it is specified. Then what is attributed to Imam al-Shafiʿi... If it were true, then the understood from our saying 'He owes me ten except three' would be 'ten, not three from it' or 'what is above seven to ten is one,' and that is contrary to what is understood in custom, so understand. And it would entail that in 'one thousand except four' it would be 'one thousand except four and fifty,' the thousand meaning nine hundred and forty-six, while the speaker does not pay attention to it, and it is not understood at the time of usage at all, but rather requires deep reflection after knowing the meaning. So understand and memorize. For the invalidity of this statement has become clear with the most solid proof that no doubt can refute at all. And from it also appears that there is no specification in it; rather the general excepted-from remains in its meaning, and the remainder is only understood from the composite, meaning that a composite meaning is understood that applies to the remainder. This is the fulfillment of what we promised earlier. Then when the author chose that what is meant by the excepted-from is the remainder, there is no exclusion from it, and as for exclusion from the ruling, it is not valid in anyone's view. He wanted to verify that and said: Then there is no exclusion of the excepted (from the ruling on all) from the excepted-from (also), just as there is no exclusion from it, since there is no ruling except on seven (by agreement). So there is no ruling on ten such that exclusion occurs from it, lest contradiction arise, for then ten would be affirmed and negated. So there is no exclusion from the ruling mentioned in the beginning, except as a stipulation meaning 'were it not for it, it would enter', i.e., were it not for the exception, the excepted would enter into the ruling. So exception prevents the entrance of the excepted into the ruling. Thus ten is only used in the compound to convey that the ruling mentioned in the beginning applies only to seven. So reflect deeply, and this is clear. But his method comes either that ten is in its meaning and seven is understood from the composite, or that it is used for seven. The truth is the first, and the author's choice is the second. He argued for this doctrine that ten in its entirety is not intended because he only acknowledged seven (by agreement), and if ten in its entirety were intended, acknowledgment of it would be necessary. It is answered that acknowledgment is only with respect to attribution, and there is no attribution except after exclusion. So its being an acknowledgment of seven does not necessitate that ten is not in its meaning, for the attribution is to what remains after the exclusion of three, so there is no approximation. So reflect. And a group, among them Shaykh Ibn al-Hajib, said: The intended is ten individuals, but he excluded three from it, then attributed to the remainder. This admits two aspects: First, that he uses ten in its complete meaning, and attributes to a part of its meaning understood within it, which is seven. Second, that it is qualified by the exclusion of three from it, resulting in a qualified composite which is 'ten reduced by three', and it applies only to seven, so seven is intended by this aspect. If Ibn al-Hajib intended the first, as Ṣadr al-Sharīʿa from us and others claimed, then redundancy necessarily follows, for mentioning the other part becomes redundant. If he intended the second, it is correct; the most that is required is expressing seven in a longer way, and there is no harm. I say: In its invalidation, the generality that justifies the exclusion may not be except after attribution, as when the indefinite occurs in the context of negation, like 'No one came to me except Zayd.' And if generality is after attribution, how can attribution be after exclusion? So reflect, for there is consideration in it. First, because this also applies to you, for the general is specified in your view before attribution, otherwise contradiction would be necessary, and there is no generality before it, so no specification. Your answer is our answer. Second, because the generality of the negated indefinite in our view is by convention, not because negation occurs upon it rationally. And if it is by convention, then what is mentioned after negation, because the attachment of negation is general before attribution, so exclusion is valid. The mentioned example is muṭlaq (absolute), so the general excepted-from is estimated and is like the uttered. And to it is what is.

Commentary
This passage is an extended usul dispute (ikhtilaf) concerning the linguistic interpretation of exception (istithna'), specifically the phrase 'ten except three' (عشرة إلا ثلاثة). The central question: does the word 'ten' in such a construction retain its real, complete meaning (haqiqah), or is it used metaphorically (majaz) to refer to 'seven'? The author (commentator of Muslim al-Thubut) refutes the latter view, which is attributed to Imam al-Shafi'i and others, and defends the Hanafi position that 'ten' remains in its real meaning, and the composite phrase 'ten except three' yields the meaning 'seven' without ten becoming a metaphor. The argument proceeds as follows: (1) The author first argues that even when a composite is reduced, the original part can still be described with a qualified expression; for example, 'ten reduced by three' truthfully applies to seven. This does not make 'ten' a metaphor. (2) He then tackles the objection that such an interpretation leads to redundancy (laghw) in speech, explaining that language allows both longer (ten except three) and shorter (seven) expressions for the same meaning, and the speaker is free to choose. (3) He argues that if 'ten' were actually a metaphor for 'seven', the word 'except' (illa) would become meaningless because it would not be excluding anything from 'ten' but rather from 'seven', which is illogical. (4) He also criticizes the attribution to al-Shafi'i, showing absurd consequences: if 'ten except three' meant 'ten not three' or 'what is above seven to ten is one', it would contradict customary understanding. Further, applying the same logic to larger numbers would yield bizarre results (e.g., 'a thousand except four' meaning 'nine hundred and forty-six'? Not understood directly). (5) The author then discusses the view of Ibn al-Hajib, who proposed two possible interpretations of the phrase. The first (using 'ten' in its complete meaning and attributing to part of it) leads to redundancy; the second (understanding a qualified composite 'ten reduced by three') is correct and merely a longer expression for seven. (6) Finally, the author engages with a counter-argument regarding generality and exception, specifically about indefinite nouns in negative contexts (e.g., 'no one came to me except Zayd'), clarifying that the generality that justifies exclusion is based on linguistic convention (wad'), not on rational occurrence. Throughout, the author maintains that the general term remains in its original meaning, and the remainder is understood from the composite construction. This is a classic Hanafi usul position that emphasizes the reality of words and the role of qualification rather than resorting to metaphor.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithnā'): Exception: a linguistic operation where a particle (e.g., illā) excludes something from the general statement.
مجاز (majāz): Metaphorical usage: using a word in a sense other than its original meaning with a contextual clue.
حقيقة (haqīqah): Real meaning: the original or literal meaning of a word when used as it was coined for.
تقييد (taqyīd): Qualification: restricting a general term by adding a condition or description.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position defended in this passage, what is the status of the word 'ten' in the phrase 'ten except three'?
A) It is used metaphorically to mean 'seven'.
B) It is used in its real meaning of ten, and the exception narrows the reference to seven.
C) It is entirely redundant and could be omitted.
D) It means 'ten' is invalid because the number changes.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school maintains that in exception (istithna'), the excepted-from term retains its real meaning, and the composite phrase yields the intended meaning without metaphor.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

10 min
The Meaning of the Excepted-From Term in Exception
Analyzing whether المستثنى منه refers to the total or the remainder

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two competing views on the meaning of المستثنى منه in exception and apply the Hanafi preferred view to interpret compound phrases.

Core Idea
المستثنى منه retains its general meaning; the remainder is understood from the composite, not from the word itself.

In exception statements like 'ten except three,' a key usul dispute arises: does the word 'ten' mean ten or seven? This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut analyzes both positions, defending the Hanafi view that the general term remains operative while the exception restricts the ruling. Understanding this subtlety is crucial for interpreting legal contracts, oaths, and acknowledgments correctly.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the two positions
Identify that the dispute concerns the meaning of the excepted-from word (المستثنى منه). One view holds it refers to the remainder (الباقي); the other, preferred by the commentator, holds it retains its general meaning.
The author of the matn adopts the remainder view.
2
Present the Hanafi argument and its defense
The Hanafi view avoids absurdities like interpreting 'a thousand except four' as 954. The commentator refutes the objection that acknowledging only seven contradicts using 'ten' fully, by distinguishing between the word's meaning and the attribution of the ruling.
Attribution (إسناد) occurs after exception removes the excepted.
3
Analyze the opponent's evidence
Examine the opponent's arguments including the pronoun reference problem (جارية إلا نصفها) and the consensus of grammarians on 'إخراج بعض عن كل'.
The commentator responds by interpreting the pronoun as referring to the linguistic concept, not the half.
4
Examine the Hanafi reinterpretation of key terms
The Hanafis reinterpret 'إخراج' as 'منع عن الدخول' (prevention of entry) to save the consensus from contradiction, and interpret 'كل' as referring to the linguistic concept, not the intended meaning.
This reinterpretation avoids the need to assume a change in the word's meaning.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf is that in the Hanafi view, the general term remains applicable in other contexts (e.g., for further specification), whereas the remainder view restricts it immediately.
This affects contracts, oaths, and acknowledgments.

المقالة الثالثة في المبادىء اللغوية اللفظ رحمه الله تعالى لو كان حقاً لكان المفهوم من قولنا له عليّ عشرة إلا ثلاثة عشرة لا ثلاثة منه أو ليس ما فوق سبعة إلى العشرة واحداً، وهو خلاف ما يفهم في العرف فافهم. ويلزم أن يكون في ألف إلا أربعة ألف إلا أربعة وخمسين الألف بمعنى تسعمائة وستة وأربعين مع أنه لا يلتفت إليه المتكلم ولا يفهم حين الاستعمال أصلاً، بل يحتاج إلى تأمل بالغ بعد معرفة معنی فافهم. واحفظ، فقد بان بطلان هذا القول بأقوم حجة لا يدحضها شبهة أصلاً، وظهر منه أيضاً أن لا تخصيص فيه بل العام المستثنى منه باقٍ على معناه والباقي إنما يفهم من المجموع بمعنى أنه يفهم معنى مركب يصدق على الباقي فهذا إنجاز ما وعدنا سابقاً، ثم إن المصنف لما اختار أن المراد من المستثنى منه الباقي فلا إخراج منه وأما الإخراج عن الحكم فلا يصح على رأي أحد أراد أن يحقق ذلك وقال ثم لا إخراج للمستثنى ( عن الحكم على الكل) من المستثنى منه (أيضاً) كما أنه لا إخراج عنه إذ لا حكم إلا على السبعة (بالاتفاق فلا حكم على العشرة حتى يخرج منه اللزوم التناقض فإنه يلزم حينئذ أن يكون العشرة مثبتاً ومنفياً فلا إخراج عن الحكم) المذكور في الصدر (إلا) تقريراً بمعنى لولاه لدخل أي لولا الاستثناء لدخل المستثنى في الحكم (فالاستثناء يمنع الدخول) للمستثنى (في الحكم ، فالعشرة إنما استعمل في التركيب لإفادة أن الحكم المذكور في الصدر (على السبعة فقط فتأمل جداً وهذا ظاهر، لكن طريقه أتي إما أن يكون العشرة على معناه والسبعة مستفاداً من المجموع، أو يكون مستعملاً في السبعة، الحق هو الأوّل، ومختار المصنف هو الثاني (واستدل على هذا المذهب (بأنه لا يراد بالعشرة كمالها لأنه ما أقر إلا بسبعة (اتفاقاً ولو كان العشرة بكمالها مرادة يلزم الإقرار بها (وأجيب بأن الإقرار إنما يكون (باعتبار الإسناد ولا إسناد إلا بعد الإخراج فكونه إقراراً بالسبعة لا يستلزم أن لا يكون العشرة على معناها فإن الإسناد إلى ما بقي بعد إخراج الثلاثة فلا تقريب فتأمل (وقال جماعة ومنهم الشيخ ابن الحاجب : المراد عشرة أفراد، لكن أخرج ثلاثة عنها ثم أسند إلى الباقي وهذا يحتمل وجهين : الأول : أنه يطلق العشرة على كمال معناها، وأسند إلى جزء معناها المفهوم في ضمنه وهو السبعة، الثاني: أن يقيد بإخراج الثلاثة عنها، فحصل مركب تقييدي هو العشرة المنقوص منها ثلاثة، وهو لا يصدق إلا على سبعة فيراد السبعة بهذا الوجه، فإن كان مراد ابن الحاجب الأول كما زعم صدر الشريعة منا وغيره فيلزم عليه اللغو، فإن ذكر البعض الآخر يلغو حينئذ، وإن أريد الثاني فهو حق غاية ما يلزم التعبير عن السبعة بطريق أطول ولا بأس به (أقول) في إبطاله قد لا يكون العموم المصحح للإخراج إلا بعد الإسناد) كما إذا وقع النكرة في سياق النفي (نحو : ما جاءني إلا زيد) وإذا كان العموم بعد الإسناد، فكيف يكون الإسناد بعد الإخراج (فتأمل) فإن فيه نظراً، أما أولاً فلأن هذا يرد عليكم أيضاً، فإن العام مخصوص عندكم قبل الإسناد وإلا لزم التناقض ولا عموم قبله فلا تخصيص جوابكم فهو جوابنا، وأما ثانياً : فلأن عموم النكرة المنفية عندنا بالوضع لا لأجل وقوع النفي عليه عقلاً، وإذا كان بالوضع فالذي يذكر بعد النفي، لأن تعلق النفي عام قبل الإسناد فيصح الإخراج، والمثال المذكور مفرغ فالمستثنى منه العام مقدر وهو كالملفوظ، وإليه فما هو

مستعملة الضمير وهذه الجماعة (قالوا) في إبطال الرأي الأول (أولاً): لو لم يكن المراد بالمستثنى منه (الكل) بل كان المراد منه الباقي لزم عود الضمير إلى النصف في نحو : اشتريت الجارية إلا نصفها لأن المذكور سابقاً حينئذ هو النصف، والضمير إنما يعود إلى المرجع المذكور سابقاً، وعود الضمير إلى النصف باطل ، إذ يكون المعنى : اشتريت نصف الجارية إلا نصفها فيكون المخرج الربع) وقد كان المقصود استثناء النصف هذا خلف ثم الربع إذا كان مستثنى بقي الربع وهو المراد بالجارية حينئذ، فيكون المخرج ربع الربع ، وهكذا إلى غير النهاية (قلنا) لا نسلم أن الضمير يعود إلى النصف بل المرجع اللفظ باعتبار المفهوم الموضوع له فالجارية في النصف والمرجع الجارية باعتبار المفهوم اللغوي وفيه نظر ظاهر، فإن حقيقة أن يعود إلى المراد بالمرجع لا إلى ما وضع له المرجع، وسيصرح المصنف به أيضاً، كيف لا وهل هذا إلا مثل أن يقال : رأيت أسداً مسلحاً، ثم يرجع الضمير إليه باعتبار الأسد المفترس، فلا يجوز إلا بالتكلف المحض المستغنى عنه، فإنه يجوز أن يستعمل الجارية في معناها كما مر ، ثم يرجع الضمير إليها فتدبر (و) قالوا :(ثانياً : إجماع أهل العربية أنه إخراج بعض عن كل ولا يمكن الإخراج عن الحكم بعد ثبوته فإنه تناقض، ولو لم يكن الإخراج عن المستثنى منه بطل الإخراج مطلقاً ويلزم خلاف الإجماع، فلا بد من تناول المستثنى منه للمستثنى (قلنا : المراد لأهل الإجماع من لفظ الإخراج الإخراج) تقديراً) بمعنى المنع عن الدخول، وكونه بحيث لولا الاستثناء لدخل فيه (و) المراد بلفظ الكل (الكلية باعتبار المفهوم) اللغوي (ظاهراً) لا باعتبار المراد وفيه أنه لا بد للتأويل من ضرورة ملجئة لا سيما في كلام أهل الإجماع فإنه لو كان مرادهم هذا المحمل البعيد لبين أحد ومن البعيد عادة أن يهمل هذا الجم الغفير في موضع الاشتباه العظيم فتدبر (و) قالوا (ثالثاً فيه أي في كون الباقي مراداً من لفظ المستثنى منه إبطال نصوصية العدد إذ صح حينئذ إرادة عدد من عدد، وهذا هو الذي مر من صدر الشريعة أقول فرق بين المفهومية والمراد بالحكم فإن معنى ربما يكون مفهوماً بحسب اللغة، ولا يكون مراداً كما في المجاز ( وليس العدد نصاً إلا باعتبار الأوّل أي باعتبار كونه مفهوماً لا باعتبار المراد وفيه أنه منع لمقدمة منقولة من أهل العربية فلا يقبل من غير حجة، والقول بكونه نصاً باعتبار انفهام المفهوم اللغوي، فليس مخصوصاً بالعدد، فإن كل لفظ في المفهوم اللغوي بمعنى هو المفهوم من اللفظ، وإن لم يرد في بعض المواضع بل النصوصية ليست إلا نصوصية الإرادة فافهم. ولا تلتفت إلى ما يبدىء احتمال كونه نصاً غير الاستثناء، قال في «التحرير» مجيباً عن هذا الوجه إن النصوصية بمعنى عدم احتمال الغير نص أنه
The third article on linguistic principles: The word. May Allah have mercy on him: If it were true, the understood meaning from our saying 'He owes me ten except three' would be 'ten, not three from it,' or is not what is above seven up to ten one? And that contradicts what is understood in usage, so understand. And it would necessitate that in 'a thousand except four' be 'a thousand except fifty-four,' with 'thousand' meaning 'nine hundred and forty-six,' while the speaker does not consider it and does not understand it at all at the time of usage, but rather needs deep reflection after knowing the meaning, so understand. And memorize, for the invalidity of this statement has become clear with the most sound proof that no doubt can refute, and it also appeared that there is no specification, but rather the general excepted-from remains on its meaning, and the remainder is only understood from the composite, meaning that a composite meaning is understood that is true of the remainder. This is the fulfillment of what we promised earlier. Then, when the author chose that what is intended by the excepted-from is the remainder, then there is no removal from it, and as for removal from the ruling, it is not valid according to anyone who wanted to verify that, and he said: 'There is no removal for the excepted (from the ruling over the whole) from the excepted-from (either), just as there is no removal from it, since there is no ruling except on the seven (by agreement), so there is no ruling on the ten such that removal from it would necessitate contradiction, because it would then entail that the ten is both affirmed and negated. So there is no removal from the ruling mentioned at the beginning, except as a stipulation meaning 'otherwise it would enter,' i.e., were it not for the exception, the excepted would enter the ruling. So the exception prevents entry of the excepted into the ruling. Thus the ten was used in the construction to indicate that the ruling mentioned at the beginning applies only to the seven. So reflect deeply, and this is apparent. But his way is either that the ten is on its meaning and the seven is understood from the composite, or that it is used for the seven. The truth is the first, and the author's choice is the second. He argued for this view: 'Because the ten in its entirety is not intended, since he only acknowledged seven (by agreement), and if the ten in its entirety was intended, acknowledgment of it would be necessary.' The response is: 'Acknowledgment is only with respect to attribution, and there is no attribution except after removal, so that it is an acknowledgment of the seven does not necessitate that the ten is not on its meaning, because attribution is to what remains after removal of the three. So there is no approximation?' Reflect. A group, including Shaykh Ibn al-Hajib, said: 'The intended is ten individuals, but three were removed from it, then attribution is made to the remainder.' This admits two aspects: First: that 'ten' is used with its full meaning, and attribution is to part of its meaning understood within it, i.e., seven. Second: that it is restricted by the removal of three from it, so a restrictive composite is obtained: the ten diminished by three, which is only true of seven, so seven is intended in this way. If Ibn al-Hajib intended the first, as Sadr al-Shari'a from us and others claimed, then it would entail redundancy, because mentioning the other part would be redundant then. If the second is intended, it is correct, though it requires expressing the seven in a longer way, and there is no harm. I say: In refuting it, sometimes the generality that validates removal exists only after attribution, as when an indefinite noun occurs in the context of negation, like 'No one came to me except Zaid.' If generality is after attribution, how can attribution be after removal? Reflect, for there is consideration in it: First, because this also refutes you, for the general is specified before attribution according to you, otherwise contradiction would follow, and there is no generality before it, so there is no specification. Your answer is our answer. Second, because the generality of the negated indefinite according to us is by linguistic convention, not due to the negation occurring upon it rationally. And if it is by convention, what is mentioned after negation is because the attachment of negation is general before attribution, so removal is valid. The mentioned example [ما جاءني إلا زيد] is of the 'mugharraq' type, so the general excepted-from is estimated and is like the spoken word. And to it is what... 

[Section on the pronoun] And this group said in refuting the first view: First: If what was intended by the excepted-from was not the whole but rather the remainder, then the pronoun would refer back to the half in expressions like 'I bought the slave girl except half of her' because what was previously mentioned then is the half, and the pronoun only refers back to the previously mentioned referent. The return of the pronoun to the half is invalid, because the meaning would be 'I bought half of the slave girl except half of her,' so the removed part would be the quarter. But the intended was to except the half; this is contrary. Then if the quarter is excepted, the quarter remains, which is then what is intended by the slave girl, so the removed part becomes a quarter of a quarter, and so on ad infinitum. We say: We do not concede that the pronoun refers back to the half; rather, the referent is the word considering the concept for which it is placed. Thus, in 'half of the slave girl,' the referent is 'slave girl' considering the linguistic concept. There is apparent consideration in it, for the reality is that it refers back to what is intended by the referent, not to what the referent was originally placed for. The author will also explicitly state this. How not? Is this not like saying 'I saw a lion armed' and then the pronoun refers back to it considering the predatory lion? That is not permissible except with pure artificiality that is unnecessary. For it is permissible to use 'slave girl' in its meaning as before, then the pronoun refers back to it. So contemplate. They said: Second: The consensus of Arabic grammarians is that it is removal of a part from a whole, and removal from a ruling after its establishment is impossible for it is contradictory. If the removal were not from the excepted-from, the removal would be invalid absolutely, necessitating violation of consensus. So the excepted-from must encompass the excepted. We say: What the people of consensus intend by the word 'removal' is removal in a notional sense, meaning prevention of entry, such that were it not for the exception, it would enter. And what they intend by the word 'whole' is the whole in terms of the linguistic concept apparently, not in terms of what is intended. There is in it that interpretation requires a compelling necessity, especially in the speech of the people of consensus. If they intended this far-fetched interpretation, someone would have clarified it, and it is far in custom that this great multitude would neglect to clarify in a matter of great ambiguity. So contemplate. They said: Third: It—i.e., considering the remainder to be the intended meaning of the word 'excepted-from'—invalidates the definitiveness of number, because then it would be permissible to intend a number by a number. This is what was mentioned by Sadr al-Shari'a. I say: There is a distinction between being understood and being intended as a ruling. For a meaning might be understood according to language but not intended, as in metaphor. And number is definitive only with respect to the first, i.e., being understood, not with respect to intention. In it is that this is a denial of a transmitted premise from Arabic grammarians, so it is not accepted without proof. The statement that it is definitive by virtue of understanding the linguistic concept is not specific to number, for every word in the linguistic concept has a meaning that is understood from the word, even if not intended in some contexts. Rather, definitiveness is only definitiveness of intention. So understand. And do not pay attention to what suggests the possibility that it is definitive other than exception. He said in 'Al-Tahrir' responding to this point: 'Definitiveness means the absence of any other possibility.' This is that.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute concerning the nature of exception (الاستثناء) and specifically the meaning of the word from which exception is made (المستثنى منه). The core issue is whether, in a phrase like 'عشرة إلا ثلاثة' (ten except three), the word 'عشرة' is used to denote the remainder (seven) or retains its full meaning (ten) while the understanding of seven is derived from the composite expression. The author of the matn (مسلم الثبوت) adopts the view that المستثنى منه is used for the remainder, following the Hanafi position held by some scholars. However, the commentator argues vigorously for the first view—that المستثنى منه retains its general meaning—and refutes several objections.

The commentary proceeds by first stating that if the second view were true, it would lead to absurd consequences, such as interpreting 'ألف إلا أربعة' (a thousand except four) as 'a thousand except fifty-four' because the remainder would be 954, but the word 'ألف' would have to mean 954, which is not the conventional usage. Therefore, the correct understanding is that the general term remains on its meaning, and the specific remainder is understood from the composite.

The commentator then addresses the author's argument that since the acknowledgment (إقرار) is only for seven, the word 'ten' cannot be intended in its full sense. The response is that acknowledgment is based on attribution (إسناد), which occurs after the exception removes the three, so the ten is still used in its full sense, but the ruling applies only to the remainder.

Next, the commentator discusses the view of Ibn al-Hajib and others, who say that the intended meaning is ten individuals from which three are removed, resulting in a restrictive composite that is true of seven. If taken as meaning the composite, it is valid but merely a longer expression; if taken as using 'ten' for its full meaning, it leads to redundancy (لغو).

A major objection raised by the opposition is based on pronoun reference: in 'اشتريت الجارية إلا نصفها' (I bought the slave girl except half of her), if المستثنى منه means the remainder (half), then the pronoun 'ها' would refer to the half, leading to infinite regress. The commentator replies that the pronoun refers to the original meaning of 'الجارية' (slave girl) in its linguistic concept, not to the half. This is analogous to saying 'رأيت أسداً مسلحاً' (I saw a lion armed) where the pronoun 'ه' refers to the predatory lion, not the armed man.

Another objection is the consensus of grammarians that exception is 'إخراج بعض عن كل' (removal of a part from a whole). The commentator interprets 'إخراج' as 'منع عن الدخول' (prevention of entry), meaning that without the exception, the excepted would be included. Thus, the 'whole' is considered in terms of the linguistic concept, not as the intended meaning.

Finally, the objection that this view destroys the definitiveness (نصوصية) of numbers is refuted by distinguishing between being understood from the word and being intended as a ruling. Numbers are definitive in the sense that they are understood, not necessarily intended. Definitiveness, according to 'Al-Tahrir', is the absence of any other possibility.

Throughout, the commentator defends the Hanafi usul position that الاستثناء is a form of specification (تخصيص) that preserves the general meaning of the متثنى منه while restricting the ruling to the remainder.

Key Terms
المستثنى منه (al-mustathnā minhu): The word from which exception is made (e.g., 'عشرة' in 'عشرة إلا ثلاثة'). According to the preferred view, it retains its general linguistic meaning.
الاستثناء (al-istithnāʾ): A linguistic operation that prevents the excepted from entering the ruling of the excepted-from. It is a form of specification (تخصيص).
الإخراج (al-ikhrāj): Literally 'removal', but in the context of exception it is interpreted notionally as 'prevention of entry' (منع عن الدخول) to avoid contradiction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the phrase 'له عليّ عشرة إلا ثلاثة', what does the word 'عشرة' mean according to the preferred view in this passage?
A) Seven
B) Ten
C) A composite meaning seven
D) Ten but with the intention of seven

Key Takeaway
المستثنى منه retains its general meaning; the exception only prevents the excepted from entering the ruling, without altering the word's semantic scope.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
12 min
The Meaning of Mustathna Minhu: Whole or Remainder?
Analysis of a usul dispute on exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three objections against the Hanafi position on mustathna minhu and explain the Hanafi responses, applying the distinction between linguistic understanding and intended meaning.

Core Idea
Mustathna minhu is the whole literally; exception 'prevents entry' not physically extracts.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the interpretation of exception (istithna) is foundational for understanding how texts are specified. A key point of dispute is the meaning of mustathna minhu – is it the whole from which a part is taken, or the remainder after extraction? This passage presents three objections against the Hanafi view (which holds it is the whole) and the Hanafi counter-arguments. Mastering this debate sharpens your ability to analyze linguistic evidence and the role of context in deriving rulings.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the core issue
Understand what is being disputed: in an exception statement like 'I bought the slave-girl except half of her', does 'the slave-girl' refer to the entire slave-girl (whole) or the remainder after subtracting the half? The Hanafi position: it is the whole. Opponents: it is the remainder.
This is a linguistic and usul question, not a fiqh ruling itself.
2
2. List the three objections against the Hanafi view
The opponents raise three arguments: (a) Pronoun reference leads to infinite regress; (b) Consensus of grammarians defines exception as extracting a part from a whole, so the whole must be present; (c) If mustathna minhu meant the remainder, numbers would lose their specificity.
Each objection targets a different aspect: linguistic consistency, authority of consensus, and numerical clarity.
3
3. Analyze the Hanafi responses
The Hanafis respond: (a) The pronoun returns to the whole in its linguistic meaning, not the part; (b) 'Extraction' is interpreted metaphorically as 'prevention from entry'; (c) Numerical specificity (nassiyya) is not intrinsic but arises from external context – the exception itself provides that context, showing a different intention.
The Hanafi defense relies on distinguishing between literal meaning and intended meaning, and on external contextual evidence.
4
4. Consider al-Qadi's view and its refutation
Al-Qadi suggests the compound 'ten except three' is a single word for seven. The author refutes this, citing infinite regress of names, pronoun issues, and composition rules.
This reinforces the Hanafi preference for treating mustathna minhu as the whole, not as part of a compound.
5
5. Conclude with the tarjih
The author concludes that the Hanafi position is correct; the mustathna minhu retains its literal meaning (whole) unless strong context indicates otherwise. The practical thamarah is how complex exception expressions are parsed in legal texts.
This dispute shows the Hanafi commitment to linguistic realism and contextual specification.

Source Text
