Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
6 min
Continuity of Suspended Divorce After Complete Dissolution
Dispute on continuity of suspended divorce after complete dissolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the majority Hanafi position that a suspended triple divorce is nullified after an immediate triple divorce and evaluate Zufar's opposing analogy.

Core Idea
A suspended divorce does not survive the complete dissolution of marriage because the condition requires the subject-matter to exist at its occurrence.

This lesson unpacks a classic usul dispute within the Hanafi school: does a suspended divorce (ta'liq) remain in effect after the marriage has been completely dissolved (e.g., by triple divorce)? Zufar argues it does, using an analogy with ownership-based suspension. The majority – Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn – hold it does not. We will walk through each side's reasoning and the key concept that a condition is a final part of the complete cause (juz' akhir min al-illa al-tamma).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position
Identify the ruling: the suspension does not remain after the marriage is completely dissolved. The husband owns only three divorces at the time of suspension; the immediate triple divorce exhausts them, so no suspension remains.
This is the view of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Identify Zufar's opposing view and his evidence
Zufar claims the suspension remains, using qiyas: just as a suspension on ownership (e.g., 'If I acquire this, you are divorced') remains even if ownership is temporarily lost, the divorce suspension should revive upon remarriage.
Zufar's analogy is based on the similarity of the suspended condition being external to the marriage.
3
Analyze the majority's rebuttal: condition as final part of the complete cause
The majority argue that a condition (shart) is a final part of the complete cause; it only becomes operative when the subject-matter (mahall) exists at that moment. Since triple divorce eliminates the mahall entirely (not temporarily), the condition cannot function. The analogy with ownership fails because ownership can be regained, but the marriage bond here is not merely suspended but annihilated.
The passage delves into whether removal of mahall is absolute or temporary; the majority view is that triple divorce removes it absolutely.
4
Examine the counter-objection and the author's preferred argument
The commentator notes a refined argument: even if we accept the principle, the simpler point is that the husband only suspended the three divorces he owned at that moment – which were immediately used up by the immediate triple divorce. The new divorces he will own after remarriage were never included in the original suspension.
This avoids the complexity of the 'final part' analysis and rests on the scope of the ta'liq.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: under Zufar's view, if the wife remarries the same husband after an intervening marriage (tahlil), she would be divorced again upon entry. Under the majority view, she would not – the condition is void.
This highlights the importance of understanding the ruling's real-life impact.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تذنيب. (التعليق هل يبقى مع زوال المحلية) للملك (فزفر) يقول (نعم) يبقى، فإذا قال : إن دخلت فطالق، فأبانها ثلاثاً يبقى التعليق كما كان حتى لو تزوّج بعد زوج آخر ودخلت طلقت قياساً على الملك) يعني إن علق الطلاق بالملك يصح ويبقى هذا مثله (والعلماء الثلاثة) الإمام أبو حنيفة وصاحباه قالوا : (لا) يبقى له أن المعلق بالشرط ليس سبباً في الحال، إنما السبب وقت وجود الشرط، وفي ذلك الوقت المحل مع الملك متحقق (أقول : وهو) أي قول أئمتنا الحق لأن الشرط جزء أخير من العلة التامة حتى لا يتوقف المعلول بعده على أمر آخر، وإنما يكون الشرط جزءاً أخيراً (ببقاء المحلية وإلا فيتوقف على أمر زائد هذا خلف (فإذا انتفت المحلية انتفت الشرطية فلم يبق المعلق به شرط وقوع الطلاق (تدبر) وفيه نظر، هب أن الشرط جزء أخير لا يتوقف المعلول بعده على أمر آخر وههنا أيضاً كذلك، فإنه بعد النكاح بعد التحلل إذا وجد الشرط يوجد الطلاق من غير توقف على أمر آخر، وأما توقفه قبل انعقاده سبباً على الغير فلا يضركما أن يتوقف بعد الإبانة بواحد على الملك، واعترض مطلع الأسرار «الإلهية أبي قدس سره أن ارتفاع المحلية رأساً يمنع الشرطية كما في حرمة المصاهرة وغيرها لعدم الفائدة وأما ارتفاع المحلية موقتاً كما في المطلقة الثلاث فلا الشرطية فقوله : إذا انتفت المحلية انتفت الشرطية ممنوع إن أراد ما يعم الارتفاع الموقت، وإن أراد الارتفاع رأساً ،فمسلم لكن لا ينفع، ثم أجاب بالبناء على مسألة الهدم أن حل المحل قد ارتفع رأساً، وهذا حل جديد حادث ،ابتداء، فإن الزوج الثاني محلل عندنا، هذا لا تخفى متانته، لكن لو رجع وقيل إن ارتفاع المحلية بحيث لا يأبى مجيء حل آخر لا ينافي الشرطية لم يبعد، فالأولى في الاستدلال لهم أن الظاهر أنه ما علق إلا ما في ملكه، وهو لم يملك حال التعليق إلا الثلاث، وقد بطلت بالتنجيز فلم يبق معلقاً، وأما الطلقات الثلاث المملوكة بعد التحلل فلم تكن داخلة في الطلاق المعلق فتدبر .
A footnote. (Does the suspension remain with the removal of the subject-matter?) Zufar says: Yes, it remains. So if he said: 'If you enter, you are divorced,' then he irrevocably divorced her three times, the suspension remains as it was, so that even if she marries another husband and then enters (the marriage with the first), she is divorced by analogy to (suspension by) ownership. Meaning: if he suspends divorce on ownership, it is valid and remains; this is similar. The three scholars, Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions, said: No, it does not remain, because that which is suspended on a condition is not a cause at present; the cause is only at the time the condition exists, and at that time the subject-matter (the wife) with ownership is realized. I say: the statement of our imams is the truth, because the condition is a final part of the complete cause, such that the effect does not depend on anything else after it. It is only a final part through the continuation of the subject-matter; otherwise it would depend on an additional matter, which is contrary (to the nature of a final part). So when the subject-matter is eliminated, the conditionality is eliminated, and the suspended matter is no longer a condition for the occurrence of divorce. Reflect. But there is a consideration: suppose the condition is a final part such that the effect does not depend on anything else after it, and here it is also like that, because after the marriage after dissolution, if the condition occurs, divorce occurs without dependence on anything else. As for its dependence before it becomes a cause on something else, it does not matter; that it depends after one (divorce) on ownership does not harm. And the master of divine secrets, Abu (qaddasa sirruhu), objected that the removal of the subject-matter absolutely prevents conditionality, as in the prohibition of in-laws and others due to lack of benefit. As for temporary removal of subject-matter, as in the thrice-divorced woman, it does not prevent conditionality. So his statement: 'When the subject-matter is eliminated, conditionality is eliminated' is rejected if he intends general temporary removal, but if he intends absolute removal, it is granted but does not benefit. Then he answered, based on the issue of demolition, that the permissibility of the subject-matter has been absolutely removed, and this is a new permissibility occurring ab initio, because the second husband is a tahlil (legalizer) according to us. This (answer) is not without solidity. But if one were to return and say that the removal of subject-matter in a way that does not preclude the coming of another permissibility does not negate conditionality, it would not be far-fetched. So the better argument for them is that it is apparent that he only suspended what was in his ownership, and at the time of suspension he owned only three divorces, which have been nullified by the immediate (divorce), so nothing remains suspended. As for the three divorces owned after dissolution, they were not included in the suspended divorce. So reflect.
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage is a dispute about continuity of suspended divorce after the marriage is completely dissolved. Zufar argues that the suspension remains, using analogy to suspension by ownership. The three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) argue it does not remain because the condition only becomes a cause when the subject-matter (the wife) is owned at that time; if the subject-matter is absent at the time of condition occurrence, the conditionality fails. The author supports the majority Hanafi view, explaining that a condition is a final part of the complete cause and requires the continued existence of the subject-matter. He considers a counterargument and a response based on the 'demolition' issue, but concludes that the simpler argument is that only the three divorces owned at the time of suspension were suspended, and those were nullified by the immediate triple divorce, so no suspension remains. This is a complex legal reasoning based on the nature of ta'liq and the hila of tahlil.

Key Terms
التعليق (al-ta'liq): Suspending the occurrence of a legal effect (like divorce) on a future condition.
المحلية (al-mahalliyya): The subject-matter that is the locus of the legal effect; in divorce, the wife's status as spouse (mahall for talāq).
الشرط جزء أخير من العلة التامة (al-shart juz' akhir min al-'illa al-tāmma): A condition is a final part of the complete cause; it cannot be separated from the subject-matter at the time of fulfillment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason the majority (Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn) reject Zufar's view that a suspended divorce survives triple divorce?
A) The husband's intention was to divorce only once.
B) The condition (entry) cannot be fulfilled after divorce.
C) The condition requires the subject-matter (mahall) to exist at the time of its occurrence, and triple divorce removes it absolutely.
D) The wife must agree to the suspension.

Key Takeaway
A suspended divorce does not survive the complete dissolution of marriage (triple divorce) because the condition requires the subject-matter to exist at the time of its fulfillment, and triple divorce annihilates the marital bond absolutely.
